commit 22047d0227ee68d47c00952604f92250e8ff0af6
Author: Vladimir Sitnikov <sitnikov.vladimir@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Jan 24 19:49:46 2020 +0300

    Add missing fork=true to Ant-based tests
    
    Note: almost all Parser-like tests had fork=true, which makes sense.
    The Parser class uses System.in to consume the input, and it
    is not a good idea to let non-forked **test** code to manipulate with System.in.
    
    The workaround so far is to add the missing fork=true, so parser executions
    do not result in System.setIn(..)
    
    See https://github.com/gradle/gradle/issues/12008

M	test/javaFiles/build.xml
M	test/javacodeLA/build.xml

commit 6dd43e978515593a12ea2fd72ad5ea9489a8fc03
Author: Vladimir Sitnikov <sitnikov.vladimir@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Jan 24 15:28:27 2020 +0300

    Fix "7.0.5" version parsing in Token.java
    
    Note: the test relies on org.javacc.parser.JavaFiles.getVersion.
    In other words, it expects that JavaCC detects "new enough" parser version
    in the generated Token.java, and it would produce "4.09+ code"
    
    It worked previously because versions had 2 components only.
    Now versions have 3 components, and Double.parseDouble fails.
    
    The workaround for now is to use only the first two components.

commit 92014421cd7e9337a9b090b69e512de630e90974
Author: Eric Spishak-Thomas <spishak@google.com>
Date:   Tue Nov 20 10:41:54 2018 -0500

    Allow empty type parameters in Java code of grammar files.
    
    This allows one to use the diamond when constructing a generic class: new ArrayList<>()
    
    This feature of the Java compiler is documented at https://docs.oracle.com/javase/7/docs/technotes/guides/language/type-inference-generic-instance-creation.html

commit b8acce67898a54498ebcd4dbf32f47f8cdc6c970

commit deabfeccd74d18763d1d051d5d09c9fc59b14b14
Author: datacompboy <datacompboy@68c0822f-77d1-6f10-b115-8a14d106ca4c>
Date:   Mon Feb 16 13:54:59 2015 +0000

    Add two options to grammar: DEPTH_LIMIT and STACK_LIMIT.
    
    DEPTH_LIMIT limits maximum recursion depth while parsing to given number.
    This check effectively limit maximum complexity of processed input.
    If you have hit this limit, consider to review your grammar for optimize.
    
    STACK_LIMIT is only for C++ target; it allows you to set hard limit on maximum
    stack usage. You can override jj_stack_check function, and define your own
    check, if you want. Default checker should be good and fast enough to have it
    always on with 90% of thread stack size you using.
    
    Additionally, destructor of SimpleNode is rewritten to be linear instead of
    recursion, so even complex trees generated by parser can be easily destroyed
    without stack overflow. But its your problem to make sure your recursive
    visitor don't make stack overflow on complex trees!

commit cf7eb202e4549ea4ac159973027208965555e292
Author: ainsleyc <ainsleyc@68c0822f-77d1-6f10-b115-8a14d106ca4c>
Date:   Sun Apr 20 07:26:27 2014 +0000

    Set the JJTREE_OUTPUT_DIRECTORY and OUTPUT_DIRECTORY on  JavaCC's own grammar definition files so that they match the folder in which they now find themselves in.
    These output directories are underneath src/main/generated-src (contrary to Francis' previous check-in).
    
    The build was working previously (as it configured the output folder via control of the execution directory), but the Eclipse Plugin needs to be able to locate
    the output folder without a context, so these modification ensure that it doesn't become confused.
    
    Also removed redundant copy of JJTree.jjt.
    
    Francis ::  I separated out the generated classes that were overridden (on the src/main/java path) versus all the other generated files on the (on src/main/generated-src path).
    The build had to manually delete the overridden classes from the generated-src path upon each build. This makes the codebase a lot cleaner because there is a clear
    distinction between curated generated classes and  default generated classes. Just dumping all classes into a single folder meant a lot of historic baggage
    (such as the 4 build scripts I eliminated).
    
    To be clear, generated classes go into src/main/generated-src , manually maintained classes go into src/main/java.

commit 481ee1253f8da1c5dbad771e34adc45d6013896b
Author: ainsleyc <ainsleyc@68c0822f-77d1-6f10-b115-8a14d106ca4c>
Date:   Fri Apr 18 04:16:50 2014 +0000

    Simplified the build as a second step towards Maven or Gradle migration (the first being following Maven/Gradle classpath folder conventions for source and resources).
    
    * Updated the Ant build so that build.xml files are no longer on the source path, and removed the parser definition files from the Java class path (ready for migration to Maven or Gradle).
    * Also removed tests from the main classpath (as is the Maven and Gradle convention).
    * Also removed generated code from the main classpath, this is not generated into its own folder, with the classes that have been overridden residing in the main classpath. This will
    make it easier to migrate to Gradle or Maven in the near future.
    * Also merged all the distributed builds into a single build.xml at the root of the project. This greatly reduces complexity and cognitive burden of understanding the build process.
    
    Work to do ... some Tests do not work (appear to be false negatives) but this is unchanged since before this check-in. The tests need work.

commit 9b6099e2ba612f73baed6008cedcd707486b3805
Author: ainsleyc <ainsleyc@68c0822f-77d1-6f10-b115-8a14d106ca4c>
Date:   Tue Jul 30 00:54:16 2013 +0000

    Improved ParseException narrative unexpected token reporting when JAVA_TEMPLATE_TYPE = "modern"; Adds a few more linefeeds, removes redundant formatting characters (extra quotes that don't mean anything), also sorts the expected token list alphabetically. In addition, will display the lexical state of the parser (very important to understand why the parser is having trouble).
    
    Old Narrative:
    
        Encountered " <IDENTIFIER> "fsdf "" at line 9, column 10.
        Was expecting one of:
            "\"" ...
            <WHITESPACE> ...
    
    New Narrative :
    
        Encountered unexpected token: "fsdf" <IDENTIFIER>
            at line 9, column 10.
    
        Was expecting one of:
    
            "\""
            <WHITESPACE>
    
        ** Lexical State : WITHIN_QUOTES_STATE

commit e44584fe817531890fadfa498e5b378fff34d88b
Author: ainsleyc <ainsleyc@68c0822f-77d1-6f10-b115-8a14d106ca4c>
Date:   Mon Jul 22 23:53:47 2013 +0000

    Significant refactoring of Options settings and the heavy use of string literals throughout JavaCC. Now all javacc options (not jjtree yet) are registered with their type and their default value, and all options are now constance with user controlled option constants (significant reduction in use of string literals) having the USEROPTION__ prefix, and options set indirectly by javacc itself having the NONUSER_OPTION__ prefix.
    
    The javacc command line help text now parses through the registry of options, and current set of default values to give the user accurate information that is guaranteed to be in-line with the code (previous approach was to manually log the options and defaults in static text within javacc which of course has become out of line with the source).
    
    Replaced OUTPUT_LANGUAGE = "gwt" with OUTPUT_LANGUAGE = "java" (which is default anyway) and JAVA_TEMPLATE_TYPE = "modern";
    
    This made a lot more sense as gwt is not a language, but rather a flavour of java compliance. The name of the option may change before relase in response to feedback, but the function (to alter the bahaviour of the code generation to decouple IO classes) will stay.

commit 3cd95c8dbdfb30057c610576677762e227457194
Author: ainsleyc <ainsleyc@68c0822f-77d1-6f10-b115-8a14d106ca4c>
Date:   Mon Jul 22 01:27:34 2013 +0000

    Updated default tab size to 4 characters from 8 characters as it was leading to
    incorrect column pointers for the majority of code. The Java standard indent is
    4 characters.
    
    Need to add a switch into the options to control the tab size from the script itself. Realistically,
    the number should always be one as the tab is just one character always and the use of tab widths
    as far as JavaCC is concerned is just for calculating the position in a column.

commit 8b9bb1ae49c95c58d2ced8e707fd9c2ff1894ffd
Author: ainsleyc <ainsleyc@68c0822f-77d1-6f10-b115-8a14d106ca4c>
Date:   Tue Jul 16 06:53:45 2013 +0000

    Integrated changes from 6.1 branch back into the mainline.
    
    This needs to be regression tested but key changes include:
    
    * A "GWT" target (which is essentially a better Java target that abstracts out the IO). This is a simple way to generate GWT compliant parsers.
    * Better exception handling. JavaCC 6.0 and lower commonly threw "Error" objects when something could not be parsed correctly. Errors tend not to be caught conventially in Java, so often a parse error would cause the entire VM to exit. Now, via use of the LEGACY_EXCEPTION_HANDLING option, this legacy can be disabled. The default value for this must be discussed and decided upon (I believe the safe behaviour should be default but that means a breaking change).
    * Going some way to remove some of the hard coding introduced when SV added C++ support. Currently the code to support C++ is very distributed throughout the code and that is making the codebase increasingly unmaintainable. This needs to be resolved before new features are added to JavaCC otherwise there will be a lot of bugs upcoming.
    
    NOTE : The 6.1 branch also contained some project folder structure refactoring which was temporarily rolled back in order to merge into the mainline. The next commit will fix the folder structure so that it matches the 6.1 Ant build scripts.
